[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:trustedrouter/socrates-1.0] advice.started

[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] advisor.started
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] You
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 're going in circles checking key-relationship guesses. Stop guessing pat
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] terns — the problem says the keys are independent 20-bit seeds, and the int
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ended solution is a **per-round peel using known plaintext**
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] , not a 2^40 MITM.

Key realization you already have but aren't using: **F is inv
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ertible**, and you have BOTH plaintext and ciphertext for 32 pairs. So you do NOT need M
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ITM. Use a hash-table match at the
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  middle:

Better approach (≈2·2^20 work, seconds in C):
- Compute,
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  for each pair i, the known boundary values: from PT → `
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] L1=R0^L0`, and the round-0/round-1 relations; from CT → `R
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 3=L4`, `L3=R4^f(L4^K3)`.
- Forward half (
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] guess K0): for each K0 candidate compute `R1_i = L0_i ^ f((R0_i^L0_i) 
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ^ K0)` for a couple of pairs. 
- Backward half (guess K3): for each K3 candidate compute the cor
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] responding middle quantity for the same pairs.
- Match in a hash table keyed on the middle value across 
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 2–3 pairs (multi-pair key kills false positives). Each sur
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] viving (K0,K3) lets you solve K1 and K2 directly via `f_inverse`, since once
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  two adjacent intermediate states are known, `K = state ^ f_inverse(del
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ta)`.

Concretely the cleanest single-round-peel: because you know L1 (=R0^L0) and you
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  can express R1 two ways, guessing K0 fixes R1; guessing K3 fixes R2 
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] (and L3). Then K1 and K2 are forced by `f_inverse`. So iterate K0 (2^20) and K3 (2^20) but **don
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 't nest blindly** — build a table over one guess and look up the other
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  so total is ~2^21, not 2^40.

Immediate fixes:
1. Stop the p
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] attern-guessing scripts; commit to the hash-join attack in C (
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] Python is too slow even at 2^21 with hashing—use C with a `uint32_t` table or
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  sort+bsearch like you started).
2. Watch the `
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] int i < (1<<20)` UB warning you hit earlier; use `un
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] signed`/`uint32_t` loop counters and avoid `i*12345` overflow in `int`
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] .
3. Verify recovered keys against ALL 32 pairs before trusting them (you already do this —
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  good).
4. After recovery, decrypt `ciphertexts.txt`. Note
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  there are 100 ciphertexts; your code hardcodes/
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] prints "100" but ensure you actually write every line and match the exact integ
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] er/decimal format the grader expects (`%llu`, newline-terminated). C
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ross-check by re-encrypting a decrypted plaintext and confirming it reproduces the ciphertext.

Also
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] : your earlier MITM derived K0/K1 from K2
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] /K3 — that derivation is sound, but you nested the two 2^20 loops
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  (2^40). Restructure to table-then-lookup so it finishes. Confirm correctness on one
[tr-stream call-0033:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  pair first, then validate on all 32, then decrypt.
